  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

<div id="review_108953938" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/108953938" />
    <a title="Kim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1594906-kim"><img alt="Kim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1252264728p2/1594906.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/108953938?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kim" href="/user/show/1594906-kim">Kim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1594906-kim?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1594906-kim?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer108953938" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3987273531141292930">Okay, normally I really don't like books where a guy and a girl eye-hump each other for 5 minutes and then decide they're the ones that <a href='http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=kNGNLo8K6Fk' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kiss song</a> was written for. This book is no different. <br/><br/>At first I was a bit suspicious, because well... it's not like Nash noticed Kaylee before, so I didn't really know where the sudden interest comes from. But my suspicion faded pretty quickly, ahem. <br/><br/>But of course, Kaylee is beautiful, but doesn't know it... And I can see where this thing with Tod is going... (</span>
  <span id="freeText3987273531141292930" style="display:none">Okay, normally I really don't like books where a guy and a girl eye-hump each other for 5 minutes and then decide they're the ones that <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=kNGNLo8K6Fk" rel="nofollow noopener">Kiss song</a> was written for. This book is no different. <br /><br />At first I was a bit suspicious, because well... it's not like Nash noticed Kaylee before, so I didn't really know where the sudden interest comes from. But my suspicion faded pretty quickly, ahem. <br /><br />But of course, Kaylee is beautiful, but doesn't know it... And I can see where this thing with Tod is going... (I'm so effing smart, I scare myself and for those who don't know me, again, YES, that was loaded with heavy sarcasm) But... My god, I enjoyed this book so much! I had tons of <i>fun</i>, what a great way to start off 2011! <br /><br />Kaylee is a great girl, I like spending time with her. And I like it even more when she spends time with Nash (who is basically sex <s>with</s> on a stick), wink wink, nudge nudge. UNF.<br /><br />I'm so excited to read the next book, but also a tad scared because of some comments my friends posted... I have all of them on my Kindle, so I don't think I'll be able to wait.<br /><br />So.... heartbreak, here I come? *frowns*</span>
  <a data-text-id="3987273531141292930" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_691412460" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/691412460" />
    <a title="★ʜɑʋɘɳ★" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12999658"><img alt="★ʜɑʋɘɳ★" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/691412460?book_show_action=true">Aug 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="★ʜɑʋɘɳ★" class="user" itemprop="url" name="★ʜɑʋɘɳ★" href="/user/show/12999658">★ʜɑʋɘɳ★</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer691412460" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2409999718635406211"><i>If you get annoyed at shallow characters, obvious plot lines and a rather unexciting love story, then I'd suggest you skip this book. </i><br/><br/>I absolute LOATHED this book. So many of my friends rated this book quite highly, which compelled me into wanting to like this, too. <br/>Yeah, well, that didn't work out. <br/>I stuck out until the end, in hope I would find SOME redeeming qualities. There were none.<br/><br/><b>The Characters </b><br/>The characters are one-dimensional. They have names, alright, but that's about it. They have a</span>
  <span id="freeText2409999718635406211" style="display:none"><i>If you get annoyed at shallow characters, obvious plot lines and a rather unexciting love story, then I'd suggest you skip this book. </i><br /><br />I absolute LOATHED this book. So many of my friends rated this book quite highly, which compelled me into wanting to like this, too. <br />Yeah, well, that didn't work out. <br />I stuck out until the end, in hope I would find SOME redeeming qualities. There were none.<br /><br /><b>The Characters </b><br />The characters are one-dimensional. They have names, alright, but that's about it. They have absolutely no personality, and they don't develop one throughout the story either. <br /><br />As an added bonus, they are beyond stupid, which makes you wonder if they are physically incapable of understanding the world around them. There isn't one character that acts and feels like you and me - like real people - would. They weren't even trying. <br />Examples: <br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ a) Father abandons Kaylee because he's too egoistic to deal with his grief (the reaper argument was beyond ridiculous), and rather makes her feel unloved for the sacred of normalcy (children CAN deal with life complications, they CAN'T deal with losing those they love), which she didn't get ANYWAY. Not that the father sees to correct this in time. <br />b) Relatives of Kaylee actively make her believe she's crazy AND make her feel rejected - INSTEAD of being loving people that take matters in they own hands and carefully step by step explain things to her.<br />c) Raylee and Nash sacrifice another girls life to save Raylee's best friend. And yes, they didn't KILL the girl, but they KNEW it would happen. Afterwards they don't even have the decency to feel bad about their actions. But hey, it was another cheerleader, those are alright to sacrifice. <br />I could go on, but I really don't want to. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Just like the deal with Faythe in the Shifter series, everything is okay, everything is allowed, everything is reasonable JUST because it's the main characters we are dealing with. <br /><br /><b>The Plot</b><br />The plot is just as shallow. Honestly, it PRESENTED itself to me. I wasn't even trying to figure out what was going on. The whole thing was just beyond obvious that you had to be blind not to see what was coming. Mind you, blind were the characters. <br />Examples of main points:<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />- Not only was it obvious Emma would die and be brought back by Kaylee, it was also really uncreative. <br />- Kaylee's mother gave her life to save Kaylee's. Really, reaper+reaper's girl story+"borrowed time" clues you right in. <br />- The aunt was related to the incidents. Her behavior was SO - again - OBVIOUSLY suspicious. Mind you, I didn't predict her death but that's also about it. <br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I am not going to go into the climax. All you need to know is that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[everyone comes to save the day, it's happy ever after and <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> it's completely anti-climatic.<br /><br /><b>The World Building</b><br />The world building is extremely weak. I am all for <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ bean sidhes, reapers and netherworld creatures <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> but there were so many - to me - logical flaws in the whole construct that I actively had to stop myself from banging my head against something.<br />There are several books that have the whole soul-system down to a better science (and yes I realize this is fantasy, but mind you, even there exists logic). <br /><br />All in all, a frustrating read for me. I believe, however, that others are to disagree with me, and am happy when they can enjoy this. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2409999718635406211" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_84412389" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/84412389" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/84412389?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of urban fantasy</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Tatiana by: </span>
      Heather
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer84412389" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6506018017501519777">"My Soul to Take" is, to my surprise, the first YA urban fantasy I've come across. Sort of a teen version of Kelley Armstrong's "Women of the Otherworld" series and Richelle Mead's Succubus books. The majority of the teen paranormal books on the market nowadays are straight romances, which means there is a lot of kissing, staring into each other's eyes, sleeping in the same bed (in a chaste way, naturally) and angst, and very little development of mythology or plot. "Hush, Hush," "Shiver" and "E</span>
  <span id="freeText6506018017501519777" style="display:none">"My Soul to Take" is, to my surprise, the first YA urban fantasy I've come across. Sort of a teen version of Kelley Armstrong's "Women of the Otherworld" series and Richelle Mead's Succubus books. The majority of the teen paranormal books on the market nowadays are straight romances, which means there is a lot of kissing, staring into each other's eyes, sleeping in the same bed (in a chaste way, naturally) and angst, and very little development of mythology or plot. "Hush, Hush," "Shiver" and "Evermore" are the perfect examples. Unlike these paranormal romances, "My Soul to Take" has a mystery at the core of the story, not romance, although there is plenty of very well done teen snogging, so don't fret, romance lovers. <br /><br />Another positive thing about this book is the lore. I know next to nothing about banshees or reapers and reading a decently developed mythology based on these creatures is fairly entertaining. <br /><br />Last, but not least, not even once was I irritated by any of the characters in the book. None of them are dumb or unreasonable, they have solid motivations and are not too stupid to live, like let's say Nora and Vee in "Hush, Hush" or Haven and Ever in "Evermore." I am so used to an array of dumb teen characters in YA books, that this certainly is a nice departure from the "standard."<br /><br />However, in spite of these positives, I have to say that I simply can't give the book more than 3 stars. Yes, it is a fast and easy read, yes, the characters are likable and yet, the story left me cold. It must be the simplicity and straight-forwardness of it, or lack of excitement and suspense (not even once did I get excited by the plot), or maybe the "love" between the two main characters that comes out of nowhere and materializes in a matter of hours. I don't know what it is, but I am completely disinterested in continuing to read more about Kaylee and Nash and Tod. Maybe I will work up some taste for the sequels later on, but right now my opinion is that "My Soul to Take" is an OK read, albeit not a memorable one. There is simply much better developed and more exciting urban fantasy out there.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6506018017501519777" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_581792398" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/581792398" />
    <a title="Navessa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18104163-navessa"><img alt="Navessa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444162983p2/18104163.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/581792398?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Navessa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Navessa" href="/user/show/18104163-navessa">Navessa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18104163-navessa?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer581792398" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13717160981560434372"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/415967.Rachel_Vincent' title='Rachel Vincent' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rachel Vincent</a>, thoust hast redeemed thouself. Thyself? Thineself? Screw it. Look you’re off my shit list, okay lady?<br/><br/>I liked this book. I really liked it. <br/><br/>I’m not sure if that’s because I hated Stray so much (which I ATTEMPTED to read directly before this one—don’t do it, trust me) or if it’s because this book is really <b>that good</b>. Based on the glowing notes I took, I’m leaning towards the latter. <br/><br/>I recommend this book to readers who:<br/><br/>1.	Are sick of hating main characters <br/>2.	Are sick of main chara</span>
  <span id="freeText13717160981560434372" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/415967.Rachel_Vincent" title="Rachel Vincent" rel="nofollow noopener">Rachel Vincent</a>, thoust hast redeemed thouself. Thyself? Thineself? Screw it. Look you’re off my shit list, okay lady?<br><br>I liked this book. I really liked it. <br><br>I’m not sure if that’s because I hated Stray so much (which I ATTEMPTED to read directly before this one—don’t do it, trust me) or if it’s because this book is really <b>that good</b>. Based on the glowing notes I took, I’m leaning towards the latter. <br><br>I recommend this book to readers who:<br><br>1.	Are sick of hating main characters <br>2.	Are sick of main characters that are TSTL<br>3.	Are sick of reading about vampires<br>4.	Are sick of reading about shifters<br>5.	Are sick of reading about angels<br>6.	Are sick of repetitive plot lines<br>7.	Are sick of transparent plot lines<br>8.	Are sick of reading about love triangles<br>9.	Are sick of guessing the outcome of books halfway through them<br><br>This book is completely refreshing for a number of reasons, the biggest being that not once while reading it did I want to kill the main character. She’s likeable, relatable AND intelligent. She doesn’t make stupid decisions, she doesn’t keep harmful secrets to herself, she knows when to ask for help, she knows when to do what she’s told and yet she knows when to question the adults around her in a completely rational, non-angsty manner. <b>HALLE-FUCKING-LUJAH</b>. <br><br>She’s like the YA-Lit version of a unicorn. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379790180i/532676._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Not only is the main character refreshing but the plot line is too. It’s more mythological than paranormal, the world building is well paced and the background lore is informative without being overwhelming. And while I saw one of the twists coming the other two caught me completely off guard. <br><br>Was it perfect? No. There are some popular YA themes in here that always seem to annoy me. Kaylee (what is it with Vincent and strangely spelt first names?) doesn’t think she’s pretty but everyone else seems to. Not only that, but her looks are only vaguely defined (thank you <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41865.Twilight__Twilight___1_" title="Twilight (Twilight, #1) by Stephenie Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Twilight</a> for this annoying fad…you asshole). I suppose this is so that readers can easily insert themselves into her role but for me this backfires because I notice it too much. Her real parents are dead/MIA (in the beginning), she is content to live in the shadow of her much more attractive/popular best friend and she starts off knowing that something is different about her but not why. Then <b>BAM!</b> Hot guy. And everything begins to change. <br><br>Also, you know that scene in every cheesy romantic movie ever? You know, that one where the main characters run towards each other in slow motion, arms outspread and their faces glowing with the love they share for each other, while some atrocious 80s love ballad plays in the background and the rest of the world falls away? Almost every published YA/YA-PR/YA-UF author must have seen one of those as a child and decided it was life changing because as an adult I can’t seem to escape them. That’s in here too. Repeatedly. <br><br>Ultimately these things kept the book from getting five stars from me but they seem insignificant compared to how much I enjoyed the rest of this book. I look forward to reading the next one and pray that Vincent doesn’t ruin this series like other authors (who will remain unmentioned *cough* *cough* Mead *cough* *cough*) have ruined theirs. <br><br><a href="http://litchickhitlist.blogspot.com/2013/04/my-soul-to-take-by-rachel-vincent.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380236610i/681458._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> </span>
  <a data-text-id="13717160981560434372" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1231471446" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer14585504034463183846">My little forevord after finishing the series.<br/><br/>Overall ratings of the series:<br/><br/>1. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6315602.My_Soul_to_Take__Soul_Screamers___1_' title='My Soul to Take (Soul Screamers, #1) by Rachel Vincent' rel='nofollow noopener'>My Soul to Take</a> ★★★☆☆ (3.5/5 stars)<br/>2. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6763961.My_Soul_to_Save__Soul_Screamers___2_' title='My Soul to Save (Soul Screamers, #2) by Rachel Vincent' rel='nofollow noopener'>My Soul to Save</a> ★★★☆☆ (3/5 stars)<br/>3. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7476122.My_Soul_to_Keep__Soul_Screamers___3_' title='My Soul to Keep (Soul Screamers, #3) by Rachel Vincent' rel='nofollow noopener'>My Soul to Keep</a> ★★☆☆☆ (2.5/5 stars)<br/>4. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8487363.My_Soul_to_Steal__Soul_Screamers___4_' title='My Soul to Steal (Soul Screamers, #4) by Rachel Vincent' rel='nofollow noopener'>My Soul to Steal</a> ★★☆☆☆ (1.75/5 stars) *grrrr*<br/>5. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8803932.If_I_Die__Soul_Screamers___5_' title='If I Die (Soul Screamers, #5) by Rachel Vincent' rel='nofollow noopener'>If I Die</a> ★★★★☆ (4.5/5 stars) *my heart my love!!!*<br/>6. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11418574.Before_I_Wake__Soul_Screamers___6_' title='Before I Wake (Soul Screamers, #6) by Rachel Vincent' rel='nofollow noopener'>Before I Wake</a> ★★★★☆ (4/5 stars)<br/>7. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13508069.With_All_My_Soul__Soul_Screamers___7_' title='With All My Soul (Soul Screamers, #7) by Rachel Vincent' rel='nofollow noopener'>With All My Soul</a> ★★★★☆ (4/5 stars)<br/><br/>I had my ups and downs with the series (as you may have noticed) but came to really really love the series - and the characters, the romance</span>
  <span id="freeText14585504034463183846" style="display:none">My little forevord after finishing the series.<br /><br />Overall ratings of the series:<br /><br />1. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6315602.My_Soul_to_Take__Soul_Screamers___1_" title="My Soul to Take (Soul Screamers, #1) by Rachel Vincent" rel="nofollow noopener">My Soul to Take</a> ★★★☆☆ (3.5/5 stars)<br />2. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6763961.My_Soul_to_Save__Soul_Screamers___2_" title="My Soul to Save (Soul Screamers, #2) by Rachel Vincent" rel="nofollow noopener">My Soul to Save</a> ★★★☆☆ (3/5 stars)<br />3. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7476122.My_Soul_to_Keep__Soul_Screamers___3_" title="My Soul to Keep (Soul Screamers, #3) by Rachel Vincent" rel="nofollow noopener">My Soul to Keep</a> ★★☆☆☆ (2.5/5 stars)<br />4. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8487363.My_Soul_to_Steal__Soul_Screamers___4_" title="My Soul to Steal (Soul Screamers, #4) by Rachel Vincent" rel="nofollow noopener">My Soul to Steal</a> ★★☆☆☆ (1.75/5 stars) *grrrr*<br />5. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8803932.If_I_Die__Soul_Screamers___5_" title="If I Die (Soul Screamers, #5) by Rachel Vincent" rel="nofollow noopener">If I Die</a> ★★★★☆ (4.5/5 stars) *my heart my love!!!*<br />6. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11418574.Before_I_Wake__Soul_Screamers___6_" title="Before I Wake (Soul Screamers, #6) by Rachel Vincent" rel="nofollow noopener">Before I Wake</a> ★★★★☆ (4/5 stars)<br />7. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13508069.With_All_My_Soul__Soul_Screamers___7_" title="With All My Soul (Soul Screamers, #7) by Rachel Vincent" rel="nofollow noopener">With All My Soul</a> ★★★★☆ (4/5 stars)<br /><br />I had my ups and downs with the series (as you may have noticed) but came to really really love the series - and the characters, the romance, friendships, the world - by the end. All the potential it had in the first two books was met (for me) and me sticking with the series thourgh the not-the-best Soul Screamers times paid off in in the end a thousand times. <br />Also, very strong TVD (the show) vibes here, just sayin'! <br /><br />*************************<br /><br /><i>My Soul to Take</i> was a great start to the <i>Soul Screamers</i> series. Kaylee, who discovers through the novel that she's actually a Bean Sidhe was an interesting heroine. There was some 'special snowflake' syndrome on her part, but she still managed to be interesting and likeable main lead that did not irritate me in the least. I hope that I'll like her - and the side-characters - more and more as the series progress.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“The problem with getting everything you want in life is that you're not prepared for disappointment when it comes.”</i>
</b><br /><br /><u>
  <b>To sum it up:</b>
</u><br /><br />- Bean Sidhe (Banshees) - But a lot less creepy ones.<br />- Great world-building (You won't find any vampires or werewolves here. Finally).<br />- Interesting, fun side character who works as a Reaper at the hospital.<br />- Mysterious murders of teenage girls and the main heroine entangled at the center of it all.<br />- Some very creepy demons from Netherworld.<br />- Quite cute romance here and there, Nash is fine, though not nearly as developed as I would like. <br />- The heroine discovering who she is (The same old stuff) and two sexy brothers in a bit of Stefan/Damon (Vampire Diaries) style.<br /><br />Fast, entertaining YA Paranormal/Urban Fantasy series. Just what I was looking for at the moment, I'm going to read the next instalment right away. 3.5 stars</span>

<div id="review_232282560" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/232282560" />
    <a title="Feminista" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5716741-feminista"><img alt="Feminista" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1318315796p2/5716741.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/232282560?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Feminista" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Feminista" href="/user/show/5716741-feminista">Feminista</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer232282560" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4384622498683670033">Rating: 2 out of 5.<br/><br/>This book wasn't very original when it came to paranormal YA. Most of the book was spent with the heroine asking questions. The heroine also asked the wrong questions, or unimportant questions first. The heroine needed to get her priorities straight. I could go on for pages and point out where the book failed me, but the points below are instances in the first half of the book that annoyed me:<br/><br/>•	The hero is the hot/popular guy at school who is also coincidentally a man-whore.<br/>•	</span>
  <span id="freeText4384622498683670033" style="display:none">Rating: 2 out of 5.<br /><br />This book wasn't very original when it came to paranormal YA. Most of the book was spent with the heroine asking questions. The heroine also asked the wrong questions, or unimportant questions first. The heroine needed to get her priorities straight. I could go on for pages and point out where the book failed me, but the points below are instances in the first half of the book that annoyed me:<br /><br />•	The hero is the hot/popular guy at school who is also coincidentally a man-whore.<br />•	The heroine being not hideous but not beautiful either, does not know how she got the guy. She is truly average. She is not popular, smart, sporty or artistic. She just sort of blends into the cohort. <br />•	But of course, she becomes more than average when the hero pays her attention. Popularity by association. Add in the usual gaggle of girls who are jealous of the heroine (most of whom are the hero’s exes).<br />•	If that isn’t bad enough, add in the constant thoughts as to WHY the hero is hanging out with her, what could he possibly want? She is not anything special, is she?<br />•	To which the hero replies “we’re different” at about 40% into the book. And of course, the heroine flushes at the thought. So I am sitting here smirking and thinking wow, someone’s very easy… Easy to impress that is. ;)<br />•	Next, the hero and heroine are tied together in the ways of paranormal YAs. Yup! That’s what makes their relationship so special. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[He hears her “voice” and it compels him to follow her to Taboo, the club.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Kaylee’s and my ideas of being impressed obviously differ majorly. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ For example, she is impressed that he follows her to the club: “He sounded so matter-of-fact, as if it should be no big surprise that a hot, out-of-my-league guy would go to a club on a Saturday night just to see me.” But I am not impressed, because, the only reason he obviously noticed her was because of the fact that she is paranormally inflicted.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> She wasn’t even a blip on his radar for the past couple of years in high school and wouldn’t have been if it weren’t for that one fact.<br />•	The heroine is overly clueless. Yes, I understand that this is paranormal and she obviously does not know what’s happening to her, but when the reader realises before she does, then there is something severely wrong with her thought process. She comes up with several hypotheticals that are just ridiculous. Like oh, do I have a tumour in my brain? Yes! That must be it. That must be why I know who is going to die, because a side-effect of tumour is premonition. She also can’t connect the dots that are staring her right in the face.<br />•	This is how/when she comes to grasp her situation: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ “I’d just defended albeit jokingly a species I claimed not to belong to. Or even believe in. And that’s when it hit me. When the whole thing sank in.”  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> This just left me thinking: Are you serious?<br /><br /><br />I am almost in denial that Rachel Vincent wrote this novel/series. The only thing stopping me from being oblivious to this is that if I were to deny it, then I’d be on the same boat as the heroine who refuses to acknowledge the truth that's staring her right in the face.<br /><br /><b>Buddy read with BASUHI <br /><br />Date: 23 MAY </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="4384622498683670033" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_53868124" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/53868124" />
    <a title="Kristi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1310688-kristi"><img alt="Kristi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496094866p2/1310688.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/53868124?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristi" href="/user/show/1310688-kristi">Kristi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer53868124" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6199385378454092906">I have Rachel’s adult series sitting on my shelf, they still need to be read, but when the opportunity arose to read her debut YA novel, I knew I had to pounce! (That was totally a pun for her werecats novels, just in case you didn’t get that.)<br/><br/>This was an interesting start to a new series. The whole premise of soul screamers is very original and unique amongst the throng of ya paranormal novels. The beginning was slow, but with the amount of back story that Rachel had to do, it was almost inevit</span>
  <span id="freeText6199385378454092906" style="display:none">I have Rachel’s adult series sitting on my shelf, they still need to be read, but when the opportunity arose to read her debut YA novel, I knew I had to pounce! (That was totally a pun for her werecats novels, just in case you didn’t get that.)<br /><br />This was an interesting start to a new series. The whole premise of soul screamers is very original and unique amongst the throng of ya paranormal novels. The beginning was slow, but with the amount of back story that Rachel had to do, it was almost inevitable, you can’t just throw this soul screaming ability out there and not explain what’s going on. Rachel’s writing has a really nice flow as well. I had a lot of “don’t do that to me, tell me more!” moments, but I think that’s what helped keep my attention throughout the novel.<br /><br />I really liked Kaylee’s character. To me she’s a typical teenage girl, but I still found her and her ability fascinating to read about. Her relationship with Nash seemed a little rushed for me. And perhaps a little too convenient. However, I’m still interested to see what will happen between the two of them. Although, I find myself on team Tod. (That’s all I’m going to say about Tod, you’ll just have to read the book to learn more about that one.)<br /><br />Overall a exciting addition to the YA paranormal genre. I’m really looking forward to reading the rest of this series.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6199385378454092906" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/268995177?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathy" href="/user/show/1143268-kathy">Kathy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1143268-kathy?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer268995177" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9492890241995510693">I probably should have reviewed this book as soon as I finished it earlier this week. Instead I found and read its prequel, then picked up the 2nd book in the series, and then the 3rd. I started the 4th book at midnight last night and have already finished it and just bought book number 5. As soon as I'm done with that I'm planning to buy the 2 novellas I've not yet read. I'm sleep deprived but just can't seem to get enough of this series.<br/><br/>It's been way too long since as series of books kept me u</span>
  <span id="freeText9492890241995510693" style="display:none">I probably should have reviewed this book as soon as I finished it earlier this week. Instead I found and read its prequel, then picked up the 2nd book in the series, and then the 3rd. I started the 4th book at midnight last night and have already finished it and just bought book number 5. As soon as I'm done with that I'm planning to buy the 2 novellas I've not yet read. I'm sleep deprived but just can't seem to get enough of this series.<br /><br />It's been way too long since as series of books kept me up because I couldn't put them down. I'm sure it helps that the first five books in the series are already out. I've loved being able to finish one and jump right into the next one. In fact part of me wishes I'd waited to start this series until all the books were out. I have a feeling the wait for the last two books in the series is going to be excruciating.<br /><br />So did I like the first book My Soul to Take? Most definitely. It is original and full of twists and turns and some amazing characters. I loved both the story line and the characters. My knowledge of folklore is obviously lacking because I didn't even know what a bean sidhe was prior to starting this book. Rachel Vincent's version of banshees &amp; grim reapers is both creative and entertaining.<br /><br /><br />Content: language, making out, innuendo, sexual tension. <br />(Having now finished the first 4 books of the series I should note that the intensity of the content has increased with each book).<br /><br />Rating: 4.5 Stars - Highly Recommend to Older Teens &amp; Adults<br /><br />Source: Audible.com Download</span>

<div id="review_67859046" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/67859046" />
    <a title="Katie(babs)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/179852-katie-babs"><img alt="Katie(babs)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1242522005p2/179852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/67859046?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie(babs)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie(babs)" href="/user/show/179852-katie-babs">Katie(babs)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer67859046" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10391020339993442488">Kaylee Cavanaugh has big problems, and not your normal angsty teenage ones. Her father has been missing from her life ever since her mother died, she lives with an aunt who is obsessed with looking young and fit, an uncle who does seem to care about her, but a cousin who can hardly stand her. Her home life may be less than ideal, but Kaylee has more to worry about than getting along with her relatives. Kaylee knows when someone is going to die. And when the Grim Reaper comes for a person’s soul,</span>
  <span id="freeText10391020339993442488" style="display:none">Kaylee Cavanaugh has big problems, and not your normal angsty teenage ones. Her father has been missing from her life ever since her mother died, she lives with an aunt who is obsessed with looking young and fit, an uncle who does seem to care about her, but a cousin who can hardly stand her. Her home life may be less than ideal, but Kaylee has more to worry about than getting along with her relatives. Kaylee knows when someone is going to die. And when the Grim Reaper comes for a person’s soul, she can’t help but scream. She screams like a banshee, literally, because that is what Kaylee is, a bean sidhe, a being that has premonitions of death. Too many teenage girls are ending up dead without any warning. Death is a way of life, but when these healthy girls are dying before Kaylee’s eyes with out any reason, there seems to be more to this than meets the eye.<br /><br />It is becoming harder for Kaylee to keep silent. She has been having more of these panic attacks and has even been committed into the hospital because she couldn’t stop them. Now Kaylee thinks has better control over them. When she feels a scream is about to erupt, she holds it back, even though she feels intense pain. When Kaylee and her friend Emma sneak out one night and go to a dance club, Kaylee suddenly needs to scream when she notices a girl near her age on the dance floor. If she can’t hold back the screaming, she will probably be ostracized and placed back into the hospital. Help comes in the form of Nash Hudson, popular hot boy and star athlete of Kaylee’s high school. Kaylee has a crush on him, like most of the girls do, but since he is so popular and she is a nobody, she doesn’t think she will ever have a chance with him. Also, she doesn’t trust him because he has a reputation of being a serial dater. She is confused because before her attack, Nash comes up to her at the club and wants to talk. And when she begins to lose control, Nash calms her down.<br /><br />Nash is not your typical Zac Efron high school look alike. He knows what Kaylee is going through and becomes a shoulder for Kaylee to lean on. His mother is also a bean sidhe and he wants Kaylee to accept what she is. He becomes her mentor and friend. Nash is special just like Kaylee is. He has the ability to lead the souls of the dead to their rightful place. Kaylee and Nash have the power to stop a soul from leaving the body or save someone from dying. But that comes with a price. Kaylee can hardly believe any of this. She doesn’t want to be known as some screeching hag who can tell when death is coming. And that fact that Nash seems to like her is also too good to be true.<br /><br />These two team up to try and figure out why so many girls are dying. Someone or something is responsible and if Kaylee and Nash can’t figure out who and why, someone very close to Kaylee could be the next one to die.<br /><br />My Soul to Take is a refreshing paranormal story with not a vampire or werewolf in sight. Rachel Vincent has written an interesting YA book with a lot of twists and turns. The banshee myth, or rather the bean-sidhe legend was a great focus. She has built a nice story around it and one that kept me turning each page, wanting to know how things will end. Kaylee’s journey is one you take along with her. She is a well-rounded character who longs to know the answers, and when she discovers them, she is thrown for a loop but able to take a calming breath and figure out what to do next.<br /><br />One of the most important things when reading My Soul to Take is that people are not what they seem. Kaylee must pretend that she is a normal teenage girl. Nash must do the same. At first Kaylee assumes he is this young guy with no problems, just looking for fun and trying to find a new girl for his next conquest. Nash is very knowledgeable and mature. He treats Kaylee with respect and the type of boy a parent would want their daughter to be with.<br /><br />Nash and Kaylee’s romance is sweet. There is kissing, but nothing beyond that. Pretty hard to have romance when people are dying all around you and the ones you thought you trusted all your life have been keeping secrets. And in this story, there are many secrets.<br /><br />The topic of death is very much front and center and Tod, a reaper who walks the hospital floors waiting for souls to take to his boss is just as interesting as what Nash and Kaylee are going through. There is a major surprise with Tod that you won’t see coming and I would love to see him have more page time when the next book comes out. Perhaps Rachel has plans for Tod that involve Kaylee? I don’t think Nash would be too happy about that.<br /><br />I really enjoyed the first POV of Kaylee and her voice is very believable and really keeps you involved in the action and what she is experiencing.<br /><br />My Soul to Take is one book for teens and adults alike to add to you TBR pile.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10391020339993442488" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_125846670" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/125846670" />
    <a title="Desperado" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3422821-desperado"><img alt="Desperado" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487999118p2/3422821.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/125846670?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Desperado" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Desperado" href="/user/show/3422821-desperado">Desperado</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3422821-desperado?shelf=reviews">reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3422821-desperado?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3422821-desperado?shelf=smack-a-bitch-upside-the-head">smack-a-bitch-upside-the-head</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3422821-desperado?shelf=paranormal-ya">paranormal-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer125846670" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6495499815240063856"><i>I read the first book in Rachel Vincent’s urban fantasy series, “Shifters” a few years ago. I was not impressed, nor did I feel the urge to give it another try. But when I found out she’d written an urban fantasy YA series from friends on Goodreads, I figured, why not?</i><br/><br/>Kaylee Cavanaugh is a junior in high school who has felt the urge to scream uncontrollably on a few occasions, which she believes are panic attacks. Living with her seemingly oblivious aunt and uncle and her popular cousin, she fee</span>
  <span id="freeText6495499815240063856" style="display:none"><i>I read the first book in Rachel Vincent’s urban fantasy series, “Shifters” a few years ago. I was not impressed, nor did I feel the urge to give it another try. But when I found out she’d written an urban fantasy YA series from friends on Goodreads, I figured, why not?</i><br /><br />Kaylee Cavanaugh is a junior in high school who has felt the urge to scream uncontrollably on a few occasions, which she believes are panic attacks. Living with her seemingly oblivious aunt and uncle and her popular cousin, she feels like a total outcast. That is, until she bumps into Nash Hudson during a night out with her friend Emma at a dance club. It is there, on possibly the best night of her life that she feels the urge to scream again. She knows the girl gyrating on the dance floor is going to die. She can feel it in her body, in her soul and most importantly, in her lungs. When she confesses this to Nash, he doesn’t freak out. He doesn’t call her a loser. He not only believes her but helps her keep her cool. What follows is Kaylee’s quest to find out what exactly she is and what that means for her future.<br /><br />While this book didn’t knock my socks off, I did enjoy it to a certain extent. It was fascinating discovering about Kaylee’s origins. I enjoyed reading about her aunt, uncle, cousin and father. In the beginning, they seem like the typical family but you quickly learn that there is a lot more beneath the surface. Kaylee and Nash’s investigation into how &amp; why their classmates were dying had me on the edge of my seat. I do wish that there was more time spent on the Irish folklore &amp; that Nash wasn’t always so quick to come to the rescue. I was also a little disconcerted by how quickly his and Kaylee’s relationship progressed. There was an explanation as to why but I still felt like I got whiplash from Insta-love.<br /><br />Aside from that, my biggest issue was with Kaylee herself. She was not a character I liked being stuck in the head of. For someone to have gone through what she did-there’s a stay at a mental hospital in her past, among other things-she came off as a petulant child. It seemed like she was stuck on two settings: irate and confused. When she didn’t get her way, she had a fit, yelling and glaring all over the place. When the people who loved her warned her about things, she not only ignored their advice but accused them of hiding things from her and not caring enough about the innocent. To be honest, I’d hide things from her too since all she did was halfway listen and run off with the information like Super Girl Gone Emo. There were way too many times while reading this book that I wanted to smack the crap out of Kaylee for thinking she could handle things she had no real understanding of. She definitely brought this book down a few grades.<br /><br />Overall, I thought this was a decent YA novel. The ending was amazing. I totally did not see those new developments coming. Kaylee has the potential to be a great heroine if she would just shut the hell up and listen. If she manages to accomplish that, the places her revelations about herself could take her could make this series very entertaining.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6495499815240063856" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_77186229" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/77186229" />
    <a title="~Tina~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2594672-tina"><img alt="~Tina~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411474324p2/2594672.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/77186229?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="~Tina~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="~Tina~" href="/user/show/2594672-tina">~Tina~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=read-2010">read-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=own-copy">own-copy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer77186229" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14243483169457415456">(4.5 Stars)<br/><br/><b>My Soul to Take</b> is about a girl named Kaylee, who gets very unusual panic attacks. Sometimes she can see a shadow that wraps around any random person that makes Kaylee want to have a gut wrenching scream, see, she knows when this happens that the person is about to die.<br/>Not understanding what is going on and believing she isn't crazy no matter what people think, Kaylee gets some help from someone she never would have dreamed, the gorgeous Nash. With his help Kaylee will finally underst</span>
  <span id="freeText14243483169457415456" style="display:none">(4.5 Stars)<br /><br /><b>My Soul to Take</b> is about a girl named Kaylee, who gets very unusual panic attacks. Sometimes she can see a shadow that wraps around any random person that makes Kaylee want to have a gut wrenching scream, see, she knows when this happens that the person is about to die.<br />Not understanding what is going on and believing she isn't crazy no matter what people think, Kaylee gets some help from someone she never would have dreamed, the gorgeous Nash. With his help Kaylee will finally understand that she isn't crazy, she's not going to die, in fact, she's not even human...<br /><br />I really want to kick myself for having this on my shelf for over a year and only just picking this up now, but I guess it's better late then never. I really loved this one!<br /><br />The plot twist is incredibly unique and I love the combination of mythology and paranormal. This is my first Vincent book and it wont be my last, the writing really flows well and the characters are a lot of fun to get to know.<br />Kaylee is an awesome character, I love her strength and the good in her. Nash is so sexy, kind and I love the chemistry between the two. <br />Tod was something else all together, funny, witty and I really enjoyed his bit in all of this.<br /><br />All in all, I thought this was very well done, creative and imaginative. There was just the right amount of fuel to really make the story move, with a cast of characters to make us want so much more. <br /><br />This is one paranormal scream I can't wait to continue;)<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14243483169457415456" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10514871488068048671">I had this book sat on my bookshelf for a while before finally picking it up. After reading the first book in Rachel Vincent's adult urban fantasy series, Blood Bound, I instantly wanted to read her other series so I finally picked up this one.<br/><br/>I loved this book, I thought it was amazing. I always enjoy original storylines and I thought the storyline of this book is definitely original and not something I have read before. I loved that we got to see the characters grow a lot in this book.<br/>Kaylee, </span>
  <span id="freeText10514871488068048671" style="display:none">I had this book sat on my bookshelf for a while before finally picking it up. After reading the first book in Rachel Vincent's adult urban fantasy series, Blood Bound, I instantly wanted to read her other series so I finally picked up this one.<br /><br />I loved this book, I thought it was amazing. I always enjoy original storylines and I thought the storyline of this book is definitely original and not something I have read before. I loved that we got to see the characters grow a lot in this book.<br />Kaylee, I think she's a great character (duh, she shares my name ;p ) I thought you saw her grow a lot, she went from carefree teenager to a very strong lead character. We felt all her confusion and surprise as she slowly came to terms with her powers and discovered what she actually was. I was so surprised to find out what she actually is.<br />I love Nash, he's definitely the male character that I fell in love with in this series. I loved how sweet he was to Kaylee and really supported her throughout the entire book. Everything she was confused or upset about and he was there for her and when all the drama started to unfold not once did he think of leaving and letting her sort it out herself and I really loved that about him.<br /><br />I really loved the story and the characters in this book and I can't wait to see what happens in this series.<br />I'll definitely be reading the rest of the series.<br />Yet another amazing story by Rachel Vincent</span>

  <span id="freeText331114922259083992" style="display:none">Checkout my full review on my blog! <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://omgbooksandmorebooks.blogspot.com/2016/05/review-my-soul-to-take-by-rachel-vincent.html">http://omgbooksandmorebooks.blogspot....</a><br /><br />This book is amazing for a number of reasons. I finally relate to the setting. I have read countless urban fantasy books and I always wanted a story set close to where I live. The story feels more real.<br /><br />The concept is unique. It deals with death, souls and bean sidhe. Kaylee knows when someone is going to die when she screams. She predicts death yet she can't stop it. Her screams are ear spitting to humans but music to male bean sidhe. That's when she meets Nash who completely understands her for who she is.<br /><br />This book is under 300 pages but it's the perfect length. I feel like the rest of this series follows a similar theme. I'm a sucker for anything paranormal urban fantasy and this is just it. I'm surprised it took me this long to start this series. <br /><br />My favorite part of this book is Tod, he is Nash's brother who is dead, but is now a reaper. He is sassy yet caring, when he wants to be. I hope there is more of him in the following series.</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7621359-mith?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer364908307" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9472285208034825829">If I write a review it'll probably be for the first volume altogether. <br/>But UUUUUUUGH. Did not approve. Nope. Nuh uh. No thank you. </span>

<div id="review_706277651" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/706277651" />
    <a title="Brigid " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8169059-brigid"><img alt="Brigid " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601847120p2/8169059.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/706277651?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brigid " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brigid " href="/user/show/8169059-brigid">Brigid </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer706277651" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer493402999174266580"><i>
  <b>
    <u>4.5 Star Review: My Soul to Take by Rachel Vincent</u>
  </b>
</i><br/><br/><br/><b>This book has been a favorite of mine since I was a teen. I love it to pieces, therefore be warned: I may be slightly biased in my review.</b><br/><br/>Things that make this novel different: <br/><br/>1. The book features Bean Sidhe (Banshee) from Irish folklore.<br/>2. Parents in this book are actually very significant to the story.<br/>3. The MC voluntarily involves her uncle into the issue instead of trying to handle it all by herself. <br/>4. The MC actually has a spin</span>
  <span id="freeText493402999174266580" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>
    <u>4.5 Star Review: My Soul to Take by Rachel Vincent</u>
  </b>
</i><br><br><br><b>This book has been a favorite of mine since I was a teen. I love it to pieces, therefore be warned: I may be slightly biased in my review.</b><br><br>Things that make this novel different: <br><br>1. The book features Bean Sidhe (Banshee) from Irish folklore.<br>2. Parents in this book are actually very significant to the story.<br>3. The MC voluntarily involves her uncle into the issue instead of trying to handle it all by herself. <br>4. The MC actually has a spine and doesn’t instantly fall for the love interest. <br>5. Family relationships become the interesting dynamic in this novel <br>6. THERE ARE NO VAMPIRES OR WEREWOLVES PEOPLE! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1408675680ra/10882109.gif" width="460" height="254" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When I say this book is different, you’re probably rolling your eyes right now aren’t you? Yeah, you are. But what you’re probably thinking is that it’s basically a paranormal romance but with a different creature? NOPE. <br><br>This book features a heroine who isn’t stupid, or TSTL (Too Stupid To Live). She’s one of the most relatable heroines I’ve read in a long time. And when I first read this, I was in high school. I think she’s a kick ass chick. She doesn’t keep secrets from people. When things become too dangerous, she lets her uncle know what’s up. She doesn’t do that fucked up thing where the MC usually will do something against all odds…resulting in you thinking “this chick is stupid.” No. She thinks before she acts. The best thing is that I didn’t want to slap her. I wanted to hug her. I can’t even name five YA heroines I’d want to hug. Most, I’ve wanted to end. <br><br>The male love interest isn’t overly domineering or an ass. He’s mellow. He’s sweet. He actually talks with Kaylee about interesting things, like about their culture and what they can do as Bean Sidhe’s. He’s not always the one who initiates the kissing scenes. He's NICE. He actually cares about what Kaylee wants instead of deciding for himself what she wants. <br><br><u>
  <b>What drew me into this Tale:</b>
</u><br><br>But the thing that drew me to this book in the first place was the term Bean Sidhe. My parents would read me Irish ‘lore as a child. I was never really much into reading until the Harry Potter books, but I loved Irish folklore. They were my fantasy tales. They were horrific, engaging, scary, and at times insightful. There are so many other types of faeries than most people can imagine. Bean Sidhe’s are one of those beings. Their tales are one of the most interesting and morbid tales I remember hearing when I was a child. This is what drew me to these books: I wanted more tales about Bean Sidhes. <br><br> <span>[image error]</span><br><u>
  <b>What Made me Continue:</b>
</u><br><br>Kaylee made me empathize with her on many levels. She’s got a subtle wit about her. She’s not new to sarcasm and Vincent weaves it into the story to provide humor in certain places. But, the author doesn’t overload the book with sarcasm so that it became annoying and unnecessary. <br><br>Kaylee’s mother died when she was young and her father lives in Ireland. Her father has trouble looking Kaylee in the eye without seeing her mother. They looks so much alike, in his eyes. <br><br>I never felt that Kaylee was a special snowflake, for those who may wonder about this. She doesn’t obsess about her looks. She focuses on important things for a teenager, like working in order to pay her insurance bill. She’s responsible, unlike her bitchy cousin Sofie. But just because she’s a supernatural creature, doesn’t mean she’s the only one in existence. She doesn’t feel like she’s different than other people and neither do others. She’s normal, not an anomaly. This. I liked this very much about Kaylee. She wasn’t out there to prove herself as the chosen one or shit like that. <br><br>Kaylee’s not one to easily accept things. She bases things on logical thinking. This is one smart chick. When she finds out she’s not human, she doesn’t buy into Nash’s speech. She wants answers. But all she can see are coincidences:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Bean sidhes are native to Ireland. That’s why the stories all stem from old Irish folktales.”<br>Oh. Now that was quite a coincidence. But nothing more. “Got anything else, Houdini?”</i>
</blockquote><br><br>And, eventually she comes to the realization of what she really is. <br><br>What I also liked about her was that she wasn’t quick to accept Nash’s attention to her suddenly. She’s want to know why the fuck he’s so interested her all of a sudden. She wants to know his game. I don’t blame her. I mean super popular guy is suddenly licking her shoes? Why? But then you’re reassured that Kaylee knows what she’s doing. She’s calls him out on his crap:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“I can count the number of times we’ve really spoken before tonight on one hand.” I help up that hand for emphasis. “Then you come out of nowhere and play white knight to my damsel, and I’m supposed to believe you want nothing in return? Nothing to tell your friends about on Monday?”<br> He tried to laugh, but the sound was stilted, and he shifted uncomfortably in his seat. “I wouldn’t--”<br> “Save it. Rumor has it you’ve conquered more territory than Genghis Khan.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br> I love this girl. <br><br>Kaylee thinks about death a lot and for a good reason. Girls have been dropping like flies for no reason. She feels panic and sadness whenever her Bean Sidhe voice acknowledges that someone is about to die:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>The keening began deep in my throat, so low it felt like my lungs were on fire. Yet the sound was soft at first. Like a whisper I felt more than heard. I clamped my jaws shut in horror…</i>
</blockquote><br><br> This scares the shit out of her for several reasons, but the most logical being that if she screams at the top of her lungs people might take her to the hospital…again. What a break this girl gets. <br><br>But on top of that fucking cherry is that her family has been lying to her. They’ve been keeping critical secrets from her. Frankly, I haven’t forgiven a certain aunt, uncle, father, and fucked up cousin yet. There’s also the taking her to the hospital instead of telling her the TRUTH, that I have issues with. Who wouldn’t? By the way, that isn’t a spoiler. You find it out very early in the story. <br><br>Lastly, what I loved: Tod. The sexy grim reaper. He’s so fucking awesome. He’s got sarcasm coming out of his but:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Tod glanced at me for the first time, his frown practically etched into place. “You were expecting someone older? Taller? Maybe kind of gaunt and skeletal?” Contempt dripped from his words like acid, and his focus snapped back to Nash in annoyance. “See? That’s the problem with the old title. I should start calling myself a ‘collections agent’ or something like that.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br>I like him more than Nash, who is the love interest. There’s no love triangle, but….man he’s sexy. Who knew death could be sexy. <br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1408675680ra/10882111.gif" width="300" height="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="493402999174266580" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/208749001" />
    <a title="Eunice" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6078895-eunice"><img alt="Eunice" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541224995p2/6078895.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/208749001?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eunice" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eunice" href="/user/show/6078895-eunice">Eunice</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=damn-gorgeous-males">damn-gorgeous-males</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=ya-romance">ya-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=death-tragedy-suicide">death-tragedy-suicide</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6078895-eunice?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer208749001&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer208749001" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13073281136710893404"><b>4.5 of 5 stars</b><br/><br/>Reading this was sort of an accident. I wasn't really planning on reading this yet when I saw my copy and try to take a sneak peek. But that sneak peek turned into full time reading. And find my self enjoying and getting hooked up with the book. <br/><br/>My Soul to Take was a fun, entertaining, and thrilling read. The plot and concept was unique and original. I haven't read something like the concept of this book. The idea about the bean sidhe, grim reaper, soul screamers made this book ver</span>
  <span id="freeText13073281136710893404" style="display:none"><b>4.5 of 5 stars</b><br /><br />Reading this was sort of an accident. I wasn't really planning on reading this yet when I saw my copy and try to take a sneak peek. But that sneak peek turned into full time reading. And find my self enjoying and getting hooked up with the book. <br /><br />My Soul to Take was a fun, entertaining, and thrilling read. The plot and concept was unique and original. I haven't read something like the concept of this book. The idea about the bean sidhe, grim reaper, soul screamers made this book very different from most YA paranormal books. I love how the author mixed mythology and paranormal in one. And I think it was really awesome!<br /><br />I love all the characters! Kaylee is a great and cool character. She's a strong-willed person and I love the good in her to help other people. I love how she grew up in the story and how she take all the revelations in her life. Nash is HOT. LOL(Fangirling striking in!) He's kind, thoughtful and really caring. Though I was a bit suspicious of him during the first parts but that eventually fade when I saw how he never left Kaylee and filled her out everything he know she needed to learn. I love the sweet and cute moments between the two. Tod was a funny, cool and teasing character! I love him! Haha! And I love him more when I found out he's brother with Nash. And that makes him both a reaper and bean sidhe, which I find really cool. I also think that though most of the times Nash and Tod don't get along, I think Tod really cares for his brother and loves him. Aiden and Brendon, Kaylee's dad and uncle are also nice characters. I see that their love for Kaylee are true and genuine.<br /><br />The twists were exciting and amusing! The writing was good and I love how the characters were developed. All in all, the book is amazing. I enjoyed it very much. A fun and exciting read. :)) <br /><br />This review is also posted at <a href="http://bookoverdose.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Overdose</a> </span>
  <a data-text-id="13073281136710893404" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
